Ruling on Severing Significant Portions of a Hunted Animal
Expands on conditions for severed parts of hunted game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when severed portions of a hunted animal are halal and apply the principle of impossibility of survival to determine the ruling for various cuts.

Core Idea
Severing a part so large that survival is impossible counts as valid slaughter, making both parts halal.

In this lesson, we explore a detailed scenario from Hanafi fiqh: when a hunter cuts a hunted animal into pieces, when does the entire animal become permissible to eat? The rule hinges on whether the cut is so severe that the animal could not possibly survive. Understanding this principle helps distinguish between a valid slaughter (which renders the whole halal) and a mere injury (which leaves the rest halal but the cut part haram).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize the act: cutting a hunted animal into pieces before complete death. The ruling is that if the cut makes survival impossible, the entire animal is halal. Otherwise, only the rest is halal and the severed part is haram.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on the hadith 'What is cut from a living animal is dead' and the rational principle that if the animal cannot survive the cut, the cut itself functions as a valid slaughter (dhabh).
The passage refers to this hadith implicitly.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith applies only when the severed part is taken from an animal that could otherwise live. If the cut is so severe that life is impossible immediately, the animal is considered dead at the moment of cutting, so the hadith does not apply. Instead, the cut itself is treated like a proper slaughter.
The key phrase: 'لا يمكن حياته فوق حياة المذبوح' – it cannot live longer than a slaughtered animal.
4
Apply to examples
Apply the principle: cutting in half, cutting off more than half the head, or cutting into thirds with the larger part toward the tail makes the whole halal. Cutting off a limb, less than half the head, or one-third from the leg side leaves the rest halal but the cut part haram.
The passage provides these distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قطع أثلاثاً وأكثره مع عجزه : أي قطعه قطعتين، بحيث يكون الثلث في طرف الرأس، والثلثان في طرف العجز ، (أو قطع نصف رأسه أو أكثره أو قد بنصفين أكل كلّه ؛ لأنّ في هذه الصور لا يمكن حياته فوق حياة المذبوح ، فلم يتناوله قوله : «ما أبين من الحي فهو ميت»، بخلاف ما إذا كان الثلثان في طرف الرأس والثلث في طرف العجز لإمكان الحياة في الثلثين فوق حياة المذبوح وبخلاف ما إذا قطع أقل من نصف الرأس لإمكان الحياة في الثلثين فوق حياة المذبوح. منه [1] قوله : وإن قطع ...الخ ؛ أي أكل كلّه، قال في تكملة البحر : لأنّ المبانَ حي صورة لا حكماً ، إذ لا يتوهم سلامته وبقاؤه حيّاً بعد هذه الجراحة، فوقع ذكاةً في الحال، فحل أكله، كما إذا أبين رأسه في الذكاة الاختيارية، أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : فلم يتناوله ... الخ. بخلاف ما إذا قطع يداً أو رجلاً أو فخذاً ، أو ثلثه مما يلي القوائم، أو أقل من نصف الرأس، حيث يحرم المبان، ويحلّ المبان منه ؛ لأنه يتوهم بقاء الحياة في الباقي أشار إليه بقوله : لإمكان الحياة ... الخ.
And if he cuts it into three parts with the larger part at the tail end — meaning he cuts it into two pieces such that one third is at the head side and two thirds at the tail side — or cuts half of its head or more, or cuts it into two halves, the whole is eaten. Because in these forms its life cannot exceed the life of a slaughtered animal, so the statement 'What is cut from a living animal is dead' does not apply to it. Contrary to the case where two thirds are at the head side and one third at the tail side due to the possibility of life in the two thirds beyond the life of a slaughtered animal, and contrary to cutting less than half of the head due to the possibility of life in the two thirds beyond the life of a slaughtered animal. [1] His statement: 'And if he cuts...' i.e., the whole is eaten. He said in Takmilat al-Bahr: Because the separated part is living in form but not in ruling, since its safety and remaining alive after this wound cannot be imagined, so it becomes a slaughter immediately, so eating it is permissible, like when its head is severed in optional slaughter. He indicated this by his statement: 'So it does not apply...' Contrary to cutting a hand, foot, thigh, or one third from the leg side, or less than half of the head, where the separated part is forbidden and the part from which it was separated is permissible, because survival of life in the remainder is imaginable. He indicated this by his statement: 'Due to the possibility of life...'.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous ruling by detailing cases where the severed portion is large enough that the animal could not survive, making the whole animal halal. The commentator explains that if the cut is such that the animal's life cannot be sustained (like cutting off more than half the head, or cutting the body in half, or cutting it into two pieces with the larger part towards the tail), then the entire animal becomes permissible because the cut effectively functions as a slaughter. In these cases, the hadith 'What is cut from a living animal is dead' does not apply because the animal is considered dead immediately. Conversely, if the cut leaves a portion that could still sustain life (like cutting off a limb, or cutting less than half the head, or cutting one third from the leg side), then the severed part is forbidden while the rest is permissible, as the animal could still survive. This is based on the principle that the cut must render the animal's survival impossible to be considered a complete slaughter.

Key Terms
أثلاثاً وأكثره مع عجزه (athlāthan wa aktharuhu ma'a 'ajzihi): Cutting the animal into three parts such that the larger portion is toward the tail (the 'ajz).
لا يمكن حياته فوق حياة المذبوح (lā yumkinu ḥayātuhu fawqa ḥayāt al-madhbūḥ): The animal cannot live longer than a properly slaughtered animal; i.e., it is effectively dead immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the half containing the head is halal.
B) The entire animal is halal.
C) The entire animal is haram.
D) The severed parts are haram, but the rest is halal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that if a cut to a hunted animal makes survival impossible, the entire animal is halal; otherwise, only the uncut part is halal.

Striking the Neck in Slaughter
First ruling on slaughter by striking neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for slaughtering a sheep by striking the neck from the front and from the back, and identify the condition that makes the back strike valid.

Core Idea
Striking from front: halal but makruh; from back: halal only if the animal is alive when the jugular veins are cut.

Scholars have detailed the method of slaughter beyond the basic requirement of cutting the throat. This lesson examines two scenarios: striking the neck from the front, which separates the head, and striking from the back. Each carries a different ruling based on the animal's condition at the time the jugular veins are severed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its variants
Recognize that the passage discusses two actions: striking the neck from the front (which severs the head) and striking from the back (at the nape).
2
State the ruling for front strike
The front strike is halal because the jugular veins are cut, but it is makruh because the strike reaches the spinal cord, causing extra pain.
Makruh tanzihi – disliked but not prohibited.
3
State the ruling for back strike
The back strike is only halal if the animal is still alive after the strike, allowing the jugular veins to be cut properly. If the animal dies from the strike alone, it is not halal.
The animal becomes carrion if death occurs before cutting the awdaj.
4
Identify the key condition
The decisive factor is whether the animal survives the strike long enough for the required cut. This aligns with the general rule that the awdaj must be cut while the animal is alive.
Refer to the principles in the Book of Sacrifices.
5
Derive the wisdom behind the ruling
The front strike is makruh due to the increased pain, not because it invalidates the slaughter. The back strike's restriction ensures the animal is not killed by a blow, which would be carrion.
Hanafi fiqh balances permissibility with compassion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ضرب عنق شاة فأبان رأسَها تحلّ لقطع الأوداج ويكره لما فيه من زيادة الألم بإبلاغه النخاع وإن ضربَها من قبل القفاء إن ماتت قبل قطع الأوداج لا تحل وإن لم يمت حتى قطع الأوداج حلت كما مر في كتاب الذبائح. ولو ضرب صيداً فقطع يده أو رجله ولم ينفصل حتى مات إن كان يتوهم التئامه واندماله حل أكله لأنه بمنزلة سائر أجزائه وإن كان لا يتوهم أن يبقى معلقاً بجلده حل ما سواه دونه لوجود الإبانة معنى والعبرة للمعاني.
And if he strikes the neck of a sheep and separates its head, it is permissible because he cut the jugular veins, but it is disliked because of the increased pain by reaching the spinal cord. And if he strikes it from the back of the neck, if it dies before cutting the jugular veins, it is not permissible; but if it does not die until he cuts the jugular veins, it becomes permissible as stated in the Book of Sacrifices. And if he strikes a hunted animal and cuts off its hand or foot and it does not separate until it dies, if healing and closing of the wound can be imagined, its eating is permissible because it is like the rest of its parts. But if it cannot be imagined that it remains attached by its skin, then what is other than it is permissible, but not that [hanging part], because of the existence of separation in meaning, and consideration is given to meanings.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage provides two additional rulings. First, regarding slaughtering a sheep by striking the neck: striking from the front and separating the head is halal because the jugular veins are cut, but it is makruh (disliked) because it causes extra pain by reaching the spinal cord. Striking from the back (the nape) is only halal if the animal does not die before the jugular veins are cut; if it dies from the strike alone, it is not halal because the required slaughter is not performed. This is consistent with the general rules of slaughter in the Book of Sacrifices. Second, regarding a hunted animal where a limb is cut and remains hanging by the skin: if the wound could heal and the limb could reattach, then the entire animal is halal because the limb is considered still part of the body. But if the limb is so damaged that it cannot be expected to heal and is only connected by skin, then the limb is considered severed in meaning, so it is forbidden while the rest is halal. This is based on the principle that legal rulings follow meanings and realities, not mere appearances.

Key Terms
أوداج (awdāj): The jugular veins which must be cut for valid slaughter.
النخاع (al-nukhā'): The spinal cord; striking here causes extra pain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sheep is struck on the back of the neck and dies immediately, before any cut is made, what is the ruling?
A) Halal because the blow was intended for slaughter.
B) Makruh but permissible.
C) Not halal; it is carrion.
D) Halal if the butcher says Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
Striking the neck from the front is halal but makruh; striking from the back is only halal if the animal is still alive when the jugular veins are cut.

Limb Hanging by Skin After Slaughter
Second ruling – limb hanging by skin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'consideration to meanings' to determine the permissibility of a limb that is cut but attached only by skin from a hunted animal.

Core Idea
A limb with no hope of healing is considered severed in meaning and thus haram, even if still physically attached.

After slaughtering a hunted animal, a limb may be cut but remain hanging by a piece of skin. Islamic law looks beyond the physical attachment to the reality of the injury. This lesson explains how the Hanafi school uses the principle of 'al-ibānah ma‘nan' (separation in meaning) to rule on such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The passage discusses a hunted animal struck such that a limb (hand or foot) is cut off but remains hanging by the skin.
2
Assess the possibility of healing
Two scenarios: (1) the wound could heal and the limb reattach, (2) the limb is so damaged that healing is impossible and it will only stay attached by skin.
The key is whether the limb can survive and reattach.
3
Apply the ruling for healable limb
If healing is possible, the limb is considered still part of the animal. Therefore, the entire animal is halal, including the hanging limb.
It is 'like the rest of its parts' – normal ruling applies.
4
Apply the ruling for non-healable limb
If healing cannot be imagined, then the limb is considered separated in meaning (al-ibānah ma‘nan). The limb is forbidden (haram), but the rest of the animal is halal.
Consideration is given to meanings, not mere physical connection.
5
Identify the legal principle
The maxim 'al-‘ibrah lil-ma‘ānī' (consideration is to meanings) governs this ruling. The essence is that a limb with no chance of survival is dead tissue, thus not part of the permissible meat.
This principle appears in many fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ضرب عنق شاة فأبان رأسَها تحلّ لقطع الأوداج ويكره لما فيه من زيادة الألم بإبلاغه النخاع وإن ضربَها من قبل القفاء إن ماتت قبل قطع الأوداج لا تحل وإن لم يمت حتى قطع الأوداج حلت كما مر في كتاب الذبائح. ولو ضرب صيداً فقطع يده أو رجله ولم ينفصل حتى مات إن كان يتوهم التئامه واندماله حل أكله لأنه بمنزلة سائر أجزائه وإن كان لا يتوهم أن يبقى معلقاً بجلده حل ما سواه دونه لوجود الإبانة معنى والعبرة للمعاني.
And if he strikes the neck of a sheep and separates its head, it is permissible because he cut the jugular veins, but it is disliked because of the increased pain by reaching the spinal cord. And if he strikes it from the back of the neck, if it dies before cutting the jugular veins, it is not permissible; but if it does not die until he cuts the jugular veins, it becomes permissible as stated in the Book of Sacrifices. And if he strikes a hunted animal and cuts off its hand or foot and it does not separate until it dies, if healing and closing of the wound can be imagined, its eating is permissible because it is like the rest of its parts. But if it cannot be imagined that it remains attached by its skin, then what is other than it is permissible, but not that [hanging part], because of the existence of separation in meaning, and consideration is given to meanings.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage provides two additional rulings. First, regarding slaughtering a sheep by striking the neck: striking from the front and separating the head is halal because the jugular veins are cut, but it is makruh (disliked) because it causes extra pain by reaching the spinal cord. Striking from the back (the nape) is only halal if the animal does not die before the jugular veins are cut; if it dies from the strike alone, it is not halal because the required slaughter is not performed. This is consistent with the general rules of slaughter in the Book of Sacrifices. Second, regarding a hunted animal where a limb is cut and remains hanging by the skin: if the wound could heal and the limb could reattach, then the entire animal is halal because the limb is considered still part of the body. But if the limb is so damaged that it cannot be expected to heal and is only connected by skin, then the limb is considered severed in meaning, so it is forbidden while the rest is halal. This is based on the principle that legal rulings follow meanings and realities, not mere appearances.

Key Terms
أوداج (awdāj): The jugular veins which must be cut for valid slaughter.
الإبانة معنى (al-ibānah ma‘nan): Separation in meaning; i.e., the limb is effectively severed even if still attached by skin, due to no hope of healing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunted animal has a leg cut off but it remains hanging by a small piece of skin, and there is no hope of healing, what is the ruling?
A) The entire animal is haram because of the injury.
B) The leg is haram but the rest is halal.
C) The leg is halal because it is still attached.
D) The entire animal is halal.

Key Takeaway
A limb cut but attached by skin with no hope of healing is considered severed in meaning and thus forbidden; the rest of the animal remains halal.

Two Hunters Shooting the Same Game: Ownership and Permissibility
Explains ruling when two hunters shoot the same game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two hunters shoot the same game, and explain how incapacitation (ithkhan) and the type of slaughter (voluntary vs forced) determine ownership and permissibility.

Core Idea
The first hunter who incapacitates the game owns it, but the game is haram if killed by a second shot when voluntary slaughter was possible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains a detailed scenario in hunting law: two hunters shoot the same game, and the ruling depends on whether the first hunter incapacitated the animal. The key is the distinction between voluntary and forced slaughter, which determines ownership and permissibility. We'll walk through the rule, its conditions, and an internal dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
State the basic scenario and split
Identify the two cases: if the first incapacitates (athkhana), the game belongs to the first but is haram; otherwise, it belongs to the second and is halal.
Incapacitation means taking the game out of the state of resistance, such that it cannot escape.
2
Identify the legal reasoning (talil)
The ruling hinges on whether the slaughter is voluntary (dhakaat ikhtiyaariyyah) or forced (dhakaat idtiraariyyah). If the first incapacitates, voluntary slaughter is possible, so the second shot is not valid, making the game haram.
Voluntary slaughter is required when the hunter can reach and slaughter the animal directly.
3
Examine the second scenario: fatal first shot
If the first shot is so severe that no significant life remains (e.g., head severed), death is attributed to the first, and the game is halal for the first hunter.
Here the second shot is irrelevant; its existence and non-existence are equal.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the first shot leaves the game with more life than after slaughter (e.g., could live a day), Abu Yusuf says the second shot does not make it haram (life negligible), while Muhammad says it does (life significant).
This ikhtilaf is between the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf, the second hunter can eat the game; under Muhammad, the first owns it but it remains haram. The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi.
Later Hanafi works often follow Muhammad's view for caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن رمى صيداً فرماه آخرُ فقتله فهو للأوّل وحرم ، وضَمِنَ الثاني له قيمته مجروحاً
إن كان الأول أثخنه، وإلا فللثاني وحل
(فإن رمى صيداً فرماه آخر فقتله فهو للأول وحرم (۱۱) ، وضَمِنَ الثاني له قيمته مجروحاً إن كان الأول أثخنه، وإلا فللثاني وحل) : أي رمى صيدا فرماه آخر فقتله، فإن كان الأول أخرجه عن حيز الامتناع فهو ملك للأول ، ويكون حراماً ؛ لأن ذكاته ذكاة اختيارية، فيحرم حيث قتله بالرمي، وإذا كان ملكاً للأول وحرم برمي الثاني فالثاني يضمن قيمته حال كونه مجروحاً برمي الأول ، وإن لم يكن الأول أخرجه عن حيز الامتناع فهو ملك للثاني ؛ لأنه قد صاده، ويكون
حلالاً ؛ لأن ذكاته اضطرارية.
[۱]قوله : وحرم....الخ ؛ لاحتمال الموت بالثاني، وهو ليس بذكاة، للقدرة على ذكاة الاختيار، بخلاف المسألة الثانية التي أشار إليها بقوله : وإلا ... الخ، وهذا إذا كان الرمي الأول بحال ينجو منه الصيد ؛ لأنه حينئذ يكون الموت مضافاً إلى الرمي الثاني. أما إذا كان الأوّل بحال لا يسلم منه الصيد بأن لا يبقى فيه من الحياة إلا بقدر ما يبقى من المذبوح ، كما إذا بأن رأسه يحلّ ؛ لأنّ الموت لا يضاف إلى الرمي الثاني ؛ لأنّ
وجوده وعدمه سواء.
وإن كان الرمي الأوّل بحيث لا يعيش منه الصيد إلا أن يبقى فيه من الحياة أكثر مما يكون بعد الذبح، بأن كان يعيش يوماً أو دونه ، فعلى قول أبي يوسف : لا يحرم بالرمي الثاني ؛ لأنّ هذا القدر من الحياة لا عبرة بها عنده.
وعند محمد : يحرم ؛ لأنّ هذا القدر من الحياة معتبر عنده، فكان الجواب في هذه المسألة عنده كالجواب فيما إذا كانت الرمية الأولى أثخنته، وكان بحال يتوهم أن يسلم الصيد منها ، فمتى رماه الثاني لا يحلّ، فكذا هذا. [٢]قوله : وضمن الثاني ... الخ ؛ لأنه بالرمي أتلف صيداً مملوكاً للأول ؛ لأنه ملكه بالرمي المثخن، وهو منقوص بجراحة ، وقيمة المتلف تعتبر يوم الإتلاف.
(۱) لاحتمال موته بالرمي الثاني ، وهو ليس بذكاة له ؛ لوجود القدرة على الذكاة الاختيارية. ينظر :
فتح باب العناية» (۳ : ۸۸).
If one shoots game and another shoots it and kills it, then it belongs to the first and is prohibited, and the second must pay the first its value as a wounded animal if the first had incapacitated it; otherwise it belongs to the second and is permissible. (If one shoots game and another shoots it and kills it, then it belongs to the first and is prohibited, and the second must pay him its value as a wounded animal if the first had incapacitated it; otherwise it belongs to the second and is permissible.) That is: if one shoots game and another shoots it and kills it, if the first had taken it out of the state of resistance, then it is the property of the first and is prohibited; because its slaughter is voluntary slaughter, so it becomes prohibited when he kills it by shooting. And when it is property of the first and is prohibited by the second's shot, then the second pays its value in the state of being wounded by the first shot. And if the first had not taken it out of the state of resistance, then it is the property of the second; because he caught it, and it is permissible; because its slaughter is forced slaughter. [1] His saying: 'and is prohibited' etc.; due to the possibility of death by the second shot, which is not a valid slaughter, because there is ability to perform voluntary slaughter, contrary to the second case which he indicated by his saying 'otherwise...' etc. This applies when the first shot is such that the game could escape from it; because then death is attributed to the second shot. As for when the first shot is such that the game does not survive it, i.e., no life remains in it except as much as remains in a slaughtered animal, like having its head separated, then it is permissible; because death is not attributed to the second shot, since its existence and non-existence are equal. And if the first shot is such that the game would not survive from it, but there remains in it more life than after slaughter, like living a day or less, then according to Abu Yusuf: it is not prohibited by the second shot; because this amount of life is irrelevant to him. According to Muhammad: it is prohibited; because this amount of life is relevant to him, so the answer in this case according to him is like the answer when the first shot incapacitated it and it was in a state where the game could conceivably escape from it, so when the second shoots it, it is not permissible, and similarly here. [2] His saying: 'and the second must pay...' etc.; because his shot destroyed a game owned by the first; because the first owned it by the disabling shot, and it is deficient due to the wound, and the value of the destroyed item is considered on the day of destruction.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding two hunters shooting the same game, including an intra-Hanafi dispute. The base rule: if the first hunter incapacitates the game (takes it out of the state where it can resist or escape), then the game becomes his property but is haram (prohibited) because it died by a second shot, which is not proper slaughter when the hunter had the ability to perform voluntary slaughter. The second hunter must pay the first the game's value as wounded. If the first did not incapacitate it, the game belongs to the second and is halal, because it is considered hunted by the second and its slaughter is forced (since the first did not disable it). The commentator then clarifies nuances: if the first shot is such that the game could survive it (i.e., escape), death is attributed to the second, so the first rule applies. If the first shot is fatal (e.g., severs the head), the game is halal for the first, and the second's shot is irrelevant. A dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad arises when the first shot leaves the game with more life than a slaughtered animal (e.g., could live a day). Abu Yusuf: second's shot does not make it haram (life remaining is negligible); Muhammad: it does make it haram (life remaining is significant, so the second shot is not valid slaughter). The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated here.

Key Terms
أثخنه (athkhanahu): To incapacitate the game, taking it out of the state where it can resist or escape.
ذكاة اختيارية (dhakaat ikhtiyaariyyah): Voluntary slaughter – the proper ritual slaughter performed when the hunter has the ability to reach and slaughter the animal directly.
ذكاة اضطرارية (dhakaat idtiraariyyah): Forced slaughter – when the animal is killed by a weapon or shot because proper slaughter is not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two hunters shoot the same deer. The first shot injures the deer but it can still escape; the second shot kills it. What is the ruling?
A) The deer belongs to the first and is halal.
B) The deer belongs to the second and is halal.
C) The deer belongs to the first and is haram.
D) The deer belongs to the second and is haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hunting law, the first hunter who incapacitates the game owns it, but if the game is killed by a second shot, it is haram because voluntary slaughter was possible; otherwise, the second owner may eat it.

When Two Hunters Shoot the Same Game
Ruling on ownership and lawfulness of game when two hunters shoot the same animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two hunters shoot the same game, distinguish between incapacitating and non-incapacitating shots, and apply the compensation rules.

Core Idea
If the first shot incapacitates, first owns it; it becomes haram if killed by the second, who must compensate.

Hunting is a lawful means of acquiring food, but when two hunters shoot the same animal, questions of ownership and lawfulness arise. This passage from the Hanafi fiqh tradition addresses precisely that: who owns the game, is it lawful to eat, and what compensation is owed. Understanding these rules requires careful attention to the condition of the animal after the first shot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario and the key condition
Determine if the first shot rendered the animal incapacitated (athkhanahu), i.e., unable to escape or be slaughtered voluntarily.
Incapacitation is the central condition that shifts ownership and lawfulness.
2
Apply the ruling based on that condition
If incapacitated → first owns, haram (second's kill not a valid slaughter), second pays compensation. If not incapacitated → second owns, halal (death by involuntary slaughter).
Compensation is only due when the first incapacitated and the second killed it.
3
Analyze the sub-scenario where the first shot leaves more life than a slaughtered animal
If the animal would live a day or less but has more life than a slaughtered animal, there is ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf says halal, Muhammad says haram.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; no tarjih is given in the text.
4
Study the compensation calculation for the case where death results from both shots
From al-Ziyadat: the second pays for his wound, half the value of the animal wounded by both, and half the meat value, reflecting the loss of the first's opportunity to slaughter voluntarily.
The compensation is not for the full animal but for the damage caused and the lost meat.
5
Connect the ruling to the underlying rationale: voluntary vs. involuntary slaughter
When the first incapacitates, voluntary slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari) is possible, so the second's shot is not a valid slaughter, making the animal haram. If not incapacitated, only involuntary slaughter (dhabh idtirari) is possible, so the second's kill is valid.
This rationale explains why the lawfulness changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن رمى صيداً فرماه آخرُ فقتله فهو للأوّل وحرم ، وضَمِنَ الثاني له قيمته مجروحاً إن كان الأول أثخنه، وإلا فللثاني وحل (فإن رمى صيداً فرماه آخرُ فقتله فهو للأول وحرم (۱۱) ، وضَمِنَ الثاني له قيمته مجروحاً إن كان الأول أثخنه، وإلا فللثاني وحل) : أي رمى صيدا فرماه آخر فقتله، فإن كان الأول أخرجه عن حيز الامتناع فهو ملك للأول ، ويكون حراماً ؛ لأن ذكاته ذكاة اختيارية، فيحرم حيث قتله بالرمي، وإذا كان ملكاً للأول وحرم برمي الثاني فالثاني يضمن قيمته حال كونه مجروحاً برمي الأول ، وإن لم يكن الأول أخرجه عن حيز الامتناع فهو ملك للثاني ؛ لأنه قد صاده، ويكون حلالاً ؛ لأن ذكاته اضطرارية. [۱]قوله : وحرم....الخ ؛ لاحتمال الموت بالثاني، وهو ليس بذكاة، للقدرة على ذكاة الاختيار، بخلاف المسألة الثانية التي أشار إليها بقوله : وإلا ... الخ، وهذا إذا كان الرمي الأول بحال ينجو منه الصيد ؛ لأنه حينئذ يكون الموت مضافاً إلى الرمي الثاني. أما إذا كان الأوّل بحال لا يسلم منه الصيد بأن لا يبقى فيه من الحياة إلا بقدر ما يبقى من المذبوح ، كما إذا بأن رأسه يحلّ ؛ لأنّ الموت لا يضاف إلى الرمي الثاني ؛ لأنّ وجوده وعدمه سواء. وإن كان الرمي الأوّل بحيث لا يعيش منه الصيد إلا أن يبقى فيه من الحياة أكثر مما يكون بعد الذبح، بأن كان يعيش يوماً أو دونه ، فعلى قول أبي يوسف : لا يحرم بالرمي الثاني ؛ لأنّ هذا القدر من الحياة لا عبرة بها عنده. وعند محمد : يحرم ؛ لأنّ هذا القدر من الحياة معتبر عنده، فكان الجواب في هذه المسألة عنده كالجواب فيما إذا كانت الرمية الأولى أثخنته، وكان بحال يتوهم أن يسلم الصيد منها ، فمتى رماه الثاني لا يحلّ، فكذا هذا. [٢]قوله : وضمن الثاني ... الخ ؛ لأنه بالرمي أتلف صيداً مملوكاً للأول ؛ لأنه ملكه بالرمي المثخن، وهو منقوص بجراحة ، وقيمة المتلف تعتبر يوم الإتلاف. (۱) لاحتمال موته بالرمي الثاني ، وهو ليس بذكاة له ؛ لوجود القدرة على الذكاة الاختيارية. ينظر : فتح باب العناية» (۳ : ۸۸). قال صاحب «الهداية»(۱) في تأويله : إنّه إذا علم أنّ القتل حصل بالثاني بأن كان الأول بحال يجوز أن يسلم الصيد منه، والثاني بحال لا يسلم الصيد منه ؛ ليكون القتل كله مضافاً إلى الثاني، وقد قتل حيواناً مملوكاً للأول منقوصاً بالجراحة، فلا يضمنه كملاً ، كما إذا قتل عبداً مريضاً وإن علم أنّ الموت حصل من الجراحتين أو لا يدري. قال في «الزيادات»: يضمن الثاني ما نقصته جراحته، ثم يضمن نصف قيمته مجروحاً بجراحتين، ثم يضمن نصف قيمة لحمه. أما الأول ؛ فلانه جرح حيواناً مملوكاً للغير، وقد نقصه، فيضمن ما نقصه أولاً. وأما الثاني ؛ فلأن الموت حصل بالجراحتين، فيكون هو متلفاً نصفه، وهو مملوك لغيره، فيضمن نصف قيمته مجروحاً بالجراحتين ؛ لأنّ الأولى ما كانت بصنعه، والثانية ضمنها مرة فلا يضمنها ثانياً. وأما الثالث؛ فلان بالرمي الأوّل صار بحال يحلّ بذكاة الاختيار أولاً رمي الثاني ، فهذا بالرمي الثاني أفسد عليه نصف اللحم، فيضمنه ولا يضمن النصف الآخر؛ لأنه ضَمِنَه مرّة ، فدخل ضمانُ ال ن اللحم فيه.
If one shoots at game, then another shoots at it and kills it, then it belongs to the first and is unlawful, and the second must pay him its value while it was wounded if the first had rendered it incapacitated; otherwise, it belongs to the second and is lawful. (Commentary:) i.e., one shot at game, then another shot at it and killed it. If the first removed it from the state of resisting capture, then it is owned by the first and is unlawful because its slaughter is a voluntary slaughter, so it is forbidden when he kills it by shooting. And if it is owned by the first and becomes unlawful by the second's shot, then the second guarantees its value in its state of being wounded by the first's shot. And if the first did not remove it from the state of resisting capture, then it belongs to the second because he caught it, and it is lawful because its slaughter is an involuntary slaughter. [1] His statement: 'and it is forbidden' etc., because of the possibility of death by the second, which is not a valid slaughter due to the ability to perform voluntary slaughter, contrary to the second scenario he indicated by 'otherwise' etc. This is when the first shot is such that the game could escape from it; because then death is attributed to the second shot. As for when the first shot is such that the game cannot survive from it, meaning only as much life remains as in a slaughtered animal, like when its head is severed, then it is lawful because death is not attributed to the second shot, since its existence and non-existence are equal. And if the first shot is such that the game would not live from it but more life remains than after slaughter, meaning it would live a day or less, then according to Abu Yusuf: it is not forbidden by the second shot because this amount of life is insignificant in his view. According to Muhammad: it is forbidden because this amount of life is significant in his view, so the answer in this matter according to him is like the answer in the case where the first shot incapacitated it and it was in a state where it could be imagined to escape, so when the second shot it, it is not lawful; similarly here. [2] His statement: 'and the second must pay' etc., because by the shot he destroyed a game animal owned by the first; since he owned it by the incapacitating shot, and it was diminished by the wound, and the value of the destroyed item is considered on the day of destruction. (1) Because of the possibility of his death by the second shot, and it is not a slaughter for him due to the existence of ability to perform voluntary slaughter. See: Fath Bab al-Inaya (3:88). The author of al-Hidayah said in its interpretation: If it is known that the killing was caused by the second, because the first was such that the game could escape from it, and the second such that the game could not escape from it, so that the killing is entirely attributed to the second, and he killed an animal owned by the first, diminished by the wound, so he does not guarantee it fully, just as if he killed a sick slave. And if it is known that death was caused by both wounds or not known, he said in al-Ziyadat: The second guarantees what his wound diminished, then he guarantees half its value wounded by two wounds, then he guarantees half the value of its meat. As for the first: because he wounded an animal owned by another and diminished it, so he guarantees what he diminished firstly. As for the second: because death was caused by both wounds, so he is the destroyer of half of it, which is owned by another, so he guarantees half its value wounded by the two wounds; because the first wound was not his doing, and the second he guaranteed once so he does not guarantee it again. As for the third: because by the first shot it became such that it would be lawful by voluntary slaughter before the second shot; thus by the second shot he spoiled for him half the meat, so he guarantees it and does not guarantee the other half because he guaranteed it once, so the guarantee of the meat is included in it.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling from Kitab al-Sayd (Book of Hunting) in the Hanafi madhhab. The passage first states the basic rule: if two hunters shoot the same game animal, the one whose shot first renders the animal incapable of escape (athkhanahu) owns it. If the second hunter then kills it, the animal is unlawful (haram) because the first hunter could have performed a voluntary slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari) but instead the animal died by the second's shot, which is not a valid method of slaughter. The second hunter must compensate the first for the value of the animal in its wounded state. If the first shot did not incapacitate the animal, it belongs to the second hunter and is lawful (halal) because its death is considered an involuntary slaughter (dhabh idtirari). The commentary then discusses three sub-scenarios based on the severity of the first wound. First, if the first wound leaves the animal with as much life as a slaughtered animal (i.e., only a twitch), then even if the second kills it, it is lawful because the first shot effectively caused death. Second, if the first wound leaves the animal with more life than a slaughtered animal but it would die within a day, then Abu Yusuf says the second's shot does not make it unlawful (since that life is negligible), while Muhammad says it does make it unlawful (since that life is significant). Third, if the first shot renders the animal so that it could potentially escape, then the second's killing makes it unlawful. Finally, the passage quotes from al-Hidayah and al-Ziyadat on the precise compensation calculation when the animal dies from both wounds: the second pays for the wound he caused, half the value of the animal wounded by both wounds, and half the value of the meat, reflecting the loss of the first owner's potential to slaughter it lawfully. The footnote clarifies the rationale: because the first could have slaughtered it voluntarily, the second's shot is not a valid slaughter, so the animal is haram and compensation is due.

Key Terms
أثخنه (athkhanahu): The first shot renders the animal incapacitated, i.e., removes it from a state of resistance and makes it unable to escape or be slaughtered voluntarily.
ذكاة اختيارية (dhabh ikhtiyari): Voluntary slaughter performed when one has the ability to slaughter the animal properly.
ذكاة اضطرارية (dhabh idtirari): Involuntary slaughter when one cannot perform the normal method, e.g., shooting a fleeing animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if the first hunter's shot incapacitates the game (athkhanahu) and the second kills it, what is the ruling and who compensates whom?
A) The animal is halal and belongs to the second; no compensation.
B) The animal is haram and belongs to the first; the second compensates for its value while wounded.
C) The animal is haram and belongs to the second; the first compensates.
D) The animal is halal and shared equally; no compensation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the key to ownership and lawfulness when two hunters shoot the same game is whether the first shot incapacitates the animal; if it does, the first owns it and it becomes haram if killed by the second, with compensation due.

Hunting Non-Edible Animals: Permissibility and Purification
Ruling on permissibility and purification of hunting non-edible animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting non-edible animals and explain how the general command in Qur'an 5:2 supports it.

Core Idea
Hunting any wild animal, edible or not, is permissible and its hide becomes pure.

Is it permissible to hunt animals you cannot eat? The Hanafi school says yes—for their skins, feathers, or even to remove harm. This lesson examines the proof from the Qur'an and the linguistic argument that the term 'sayd' (game) covers all wild animals. We will also see how hunting itself renders the meat and hide pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hunting (sayd) after leaving ihram. The ruling: for non-edible animals, the meat and hide become pure (tahir) by hunting, and the hunt itself is permissible (mubah).
The passage states: 'as for that which is not edible, by hunting its meat and hide become purified.'
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Qur'an 5:2: { وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَأَصْطَادُوا } ('And when you have terminated the state of ihram, then hunt'). This is a general command.
The verse is from Surah al-Ma'idah.
3
Analyse the scope of the dalil
The word 'sayd' (game/hunt) linguistically includes all wild animals, not just those with edible meat. The Hanafi school takes the general ('amm) as inclusive until a specific restriction is proven.
Linguists confirm that 'sayd' is not restricted to edible animals.
4
Consider the underlying benefit
Hunting non-edible animals is a means to benefit from their skin, fur, feathers, or to repel their harm. All such benefits are legislated (mashru').
The passage explicitly mentions these benefits as reasons.
5
Derive the ruling
Therefore, hunting non-edible animals is permissible (mubah), and the act of hunting purifies both the meat and hide, making them lawful to use (e.g., selling the hide, using feathers).
The meat of non-edible animals is not eaten, but it becomes pure and can be disposed of or used for non-consumption purposes.

Therefore, hunting non-edible animals (such as predators for their skins, birds for feathers) is permissible and beneficial. Furthermore, the act of hunting (istiyad) renders the meat and hide of such animals pure (tahir), meaning they can be used or sold. The proof is the general command in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:2) to hunt, which does not specify edible animals, and the linguistic scope. Additionally, there is a maslaha (public benefit) in hunting for pelts, feathers, or to remove pests. All of this is considered mashru' (legislated) in the Hanafi school.

Liability of the Mortgagee When the Pawn Perishes
Expanding the ruling on pawn destruction with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on destruction of a pawn, explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Maliki and Zufar positions, and apply the principle of yad al-istifa' to determine liability.

Core Idea
The mortgagee's hand is a hand of recovery — liability only to the extent of recovery, not beyond.

When a pawn perishes in the mortgagee's possession, who bears the loss? The Hanafi school answers by analyzing the nature of the mortgagee's possession. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the key principle of yad al-istifa', and the disagreements with Imam Malik and the Hanafi scholar Zufar. By the end, you will see how the school distinguishes between recovery and guarantee.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi rule and its three scenarios
Memorize the three cases: (1) value equals debt – debt falls; (2) value exceeds debt – excess is trust; (3) value less than debt – debt reduced, mortgagee claims remainder.
2
Identify the key principle: yad al-istifa'
The mortgagee's hand is a 'hand of recovery', not a 'hand of guarantee'. Liability arises only to the extent of recovery actually achieved.
3
Understand Zufar's opposing view
Zufar (a Hanafi dissenter) argues the pawn is guaranteed by full value, relying on the hadith of Ali (r.a.) and the concept that the excess is also mortgaged.
4
Differentiate the Maliki view on hidden vs. overt destruction
Malik holds full guarantee only for hidden destruction (like theft); for overt destruction (fire, flood), it is trust. This nuance is often missed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Apply to a real scenario: pawn worth 1500, debt 1000. Hanafi says mortgagee owes nothing extra; Maliki/Zufar say he owes 500 to the pawner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If it (the pawn) perishes while both (debt and value) are equal, his debt falls. If its value is more, the excess is trust. If less, the debt is reduced by its amount, and the mortgagee claims the excess. The conclusion is that the mortgagee's hand on the pawn is a hand of recovery because it is a security for the side of recovery, to be a means to it, so it is recovery in a sense, and it is brought near by destruction. So if the debt is less than the value, he has recovered the debt, and the excess is trust. If the value is less, he is recovering to the extent of the financial value, which is the value, so he claims the excess. This is our position. According to Malik, it is guaranteed by the (full) value. According to al-Shafi'i, it is not guaranteed; rather it is trust. If the garment's value is five, the mortgagee claims another five from the pawner. If its value is fifteen, the excess is trust according to us. [2] His statement: 'And according to Malik, it is guaranteed by the value' i.e., the full value, whether it equals the debt or is more or less. This is if the destruction occurs in a hidden manner. If it occurs in an overt manner, like death, fire, or drowning, it is trust according to Malik also. So in 'al-Uyun' and 'Sharh al-Bukhari'. And it has occurred in 'al-Hidayah' and its commentaries, and commentaries of 'al-Majma': 'Zufar' instead of 'Malik'. So let one ponder the reconciliation between them. Al-Jalabi said it. And in 'al-Hidayah': Zufar said: The pawn is guaranteed by the value, such that if the pawn perishes and its value on the day of pawning is one thousand five hundred, and the debt is one thousand, the pawner claims five hundred from the mortgagee. He has the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'They return the excess in the pawn.' And because the excess over the debt is mortgaged, since it is detained by it, so it is guaranteed in consideration of the amount of the debt. Our school is narrated from 'Umar and 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud; and because the mortgagee's hand is a hand of recovery, so it does not necessitate guarantee except to the extent of the amount recovered, as in the reality of recovery. The excess is mortgaged by necessity of preventing the detention of the original without it, but there is no necessity for guarantee. And the meaning of 'return' in what was narrated is in the case of sale, for it was narrated from him that he said: 'The mortgagee is a trustee over the excess.'
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling on the destruction of a pawn (rahn) and its effect on the debt. The commentator explains the Hanafi position and then contrasts it with the views of Imam Malik and Zufar (a Hanafi dissenter). The core Hanafi rule: the mortgagee's possession of the pawn is a 'hand of recovery' (yad al-istifa'), meaning it is held as a means to recover the debt. Therefore, when the pawn perishes, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered the debt to the extent of the lesser of the debt or the value of the pawn. If the value exceeds the debt, the excess is held as a trust (amanah) — the mortgagee is not liable for it. If the value is less, the debt is reduced by that value, and the mortgagee can claim the remaining debt from the pawner. If they are equal, the entire debt is discharged. This is based on the principle that the mortgagee's hand does not create liability (dhaman) beyond the amount recovered, unlike a buyer's hand which creates full liability. The commentator then notes that Imam Malik holds the pawn is guaranteed by its full value in cases of hidden destruction (like theft), but in overt destruction (like fire) it is trust. Zufar, from within the Hanafi school, also holds it is guaranteed by full value, relying on a hadith from Ali (r.a.) about returning the excess and the idea that the excess is also mortgaged. The Hanafi response is that the hadith refers to the case of sale, not destruction, and the excess is held as a mortgage only to facilitate detention of the principal, not to create liability. The commentator also clarifies a textual confusion: in some versions of al-Hidayah, 'Zufar' appears instead of 'Malik', and he urges the student to reconcile the two.

Key Terms
يد استيفاء (yad al-istifa'): A hand of recovery: the mortgagee's possession of the pawn as a means to recover the debt, not as an owner or trustee.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the obligation to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; property held without liability for loss unless caused by negligence or transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pawn perishes and its value is greater than the debt, what is the status of the excess value?
A) The mortgagee must pay the excess to the pawner.
B) The excess remains a debt owed by the pawner.
C) The excess is trust (amanah) and the mortgagee is not liable for it.
D) The excess is forfeited to the mortgagee.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi, the pawn is guaranteed only up to the lesser of value or debt because the mortgagee's hand is a hand of recovery, not liability.

Mortgagee's Right to Detain Pawn After Rescission
Stating the mortgagee's detention right survives rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mortgagee's right to detain the pawn after contract rescission and identify the conditions that continue and nullify this right.

Core Idea
Rescinding the pawn contract does not end the mortgagee's right to detain the pawn until the debt is paid or released.

In Hanafi fiqh, the pawn contract (rahn) grants the mortgagee (murtahin) two core rights: to demand the debt and to physically detain the pawn as security. A critical question arises when the pawn contract itself is rescinded (faskh) — does the mortgagee lose the right to hold the pawn? This lesson clarifies that rescission does not automatically terminate the detention right. Instead, the right persists as long as the mortgagee retains possession and the debt remains unpaid, ending only when the pawn is returned with the explicit intention of rescission, or the debt is paid or the mortgagee is released.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mortgagee's two core rights
From the passage, extract the two rights explicitly stated: (1) the right to demand the debt from the pawner, and (2) the right to detain the pawn as security for that debt.
These rights are established by the pawn contract and do not fall away simply because the contract exists.
2
Understand the effect of contract rescission on detention
The passage states that the right to detain continues even after rescission of the pawn contract. Note that rescission does not nullify the detention; it only ends when the pawn is returned to the pawner 'in the manner of rescission' (i.e., with the intention of ending the pledge), not merely by rescinding the contract.
The key is that rescission and return of pawn are separate acts. Rescission without return does not end the right.
3
Identify what nullifies the right to detain
The detention right ends only when (a) the mortgagee receives the debt, or (b) the debtor releases him (ibra'), or (c) the mortgagee returns the pawn to the pawner with the specific intention of rescission (i.e., ending the pledge relationship).
Simple demand by the pawner or mere rescission without return does not suffice.
4
Grasp the rationale: guarantee persists
The passage explains that the pawn remains a guarantee (daman) as long as two elements coexist: possession by the mortgagee and the existence of the debt. The detention right is tied to these substantive elements, not to the contract's formal existence.
This shows the Hanafi view that the right is a real security right, not merely contractual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمرتهن طلب دينِهِ من راهنه، فإنّه لا يسقط بالرهن طلب الدين وحبسه به ) : أي حبس الرهن بالدين، وحبس رهنه بعد فسخ عقده حتى يقبض دينه أو يبرئه) ، فإنّه لا يبطل إلا بالرد على الراهن على وجه الفسخ ؛ لأنه يبقى مضموناً ما بقى القبض والدين.
And the mortgagee has the right to demand his debt from his pawner, for the demand of the debt and the detention of the pawn thereby (i.e., detention of the pawn for the debt) do not fall by the pawn. And [the mortgagee has the right] to detain his pawn after rescission of his contract until he receives his debt or he (the debtor) releases him. For it (the right to detain) is not nullified except by returning it to the pawner in the manner of rescission, because it remains guaranteed as long as possession and the debt remain.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the mortgagee's (murtahin) rights after the pawn contract (rahn) is established. First, the mortgagee retains the right to demand the debt from the pawner (rahin) — the pawn contract does not suspend this right. Second, the mortgagee has the right to physically detain (habs) the pawn as security for the debt. This right to detain continues even after the pawn contract is rescinded (faskh), until the mortgagee receives payment of the debt or the debtor releases him from the debt (ibra'). The detention right is not nullified simply by rescission of the contract; it only ends when the pawn is returned to the pawner explicitly as a rescission (i.e., with the intention of ending the pledge relationship). The reason: the pawn remains a guarantee (daman) for the debt as long as the mortgagee retains possession and the debt remains unpaid. This ruling underscores the strength of the mortgagee's security interest: the detention is not dependent on the contract's existence but on the existence of possession and the debt.

Key Terms
حبس بالدين (habs bi al-dayn): Detention of the pawn as security for the debt; the mortgagee's right to keep the pawn until the debt is paid.
فسخ العقد (faskh al-'aqd): Rescission of the pawn contract; the annulment of the agreement that created the pledge.
براءة (bara'ah): Release; the debtor's act of freeing the mortgagee from the debt, ending the pledge relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only when the pawner demands it.
C) When the mortgagee receives the debt or is released, and returns the pawn with the intention of rescission.
D) When the pawner brings the debt to court.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's right to detain the pawn survives contract rescission and ends only with payment, release, or return of the pawn with the intention of ending the pledge.

Trustee's Option Upon Reclamation of Pawned Item
Explains 'adl's recourse and effect of stipulated agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'adl's option upon reclamation of a pawned item and distinguish the effects of stipulated versus non-stipulated agency on the 'adl's right of recourse.

Core Idea
The 'adl's recourse depends on whether the agency was stipulated in the pawn contract.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the legal options available to the 'adl (trustee) when a pawned item is sold and later reclaimed by a third party. It introduces a crucial distinction: if the agency to sell was stipulated in the pawn contract, the 'adl may choose to seek compensation from either the pledgor or the mortgagee; but if the agency was not stipulated, recourse is only against the pledgor. The passage also reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether such an agent can be compelled to sell.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and events
Recognize the roles: mustahiqq (claimant), purchaser, 'adl, rahin (pledgor), murtahin (mortgagee). Understand the sequence: pawn sold, reclaimed, purchaser sues 'adl, 'adl seeks recourse.
The claimant takes the item from the purchaser; the purchaser then sues the 'adl for the price.
2
State the 'adl's basic option
When the pawn is reclaimed, the 'adl can either hold the pledgor liable for the price (then the mortgagee's receipt is valid) or hold the mortgagee liable (then the mortgagee recovers from the pledgor).
The option is described as 'al-‘adl bil-khiyār'.
3
Distinguish stipulated vs. non-stipulated agency
Note that the option exists only if the agency was stipulated in the pawn contract. If not stipulated, the 'adl's recourse is solely against the pledgor, regardless of who received the price.
The key phrase: 'wa in lam yushtarat al-tawkīl fī al-raj‘a...'
4
Explain the legal reasoning
The mortgagee's right becomes attached to the agency if stipulated, making him liable. If not, it is like a separate agency where the agent cannot sue the recipient.
This is based on the principle that the mortgagee's consent to the pawn without agency is complete.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Sarakhsi holds the agent cannot be compelled (zahir al-riwaya), while Fakhr al-Islam holds compulsion is possible (asahh).
The tarjih leans toward the latter, but the matter remains disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

، وحينئذ صح قبض المرتهن الثمن، وإمّا أن يرجع على المرتهن ، ثم المرتهن يرجعُ على الراهن بدينه. قوله : أداه إليه ؛ لأنه تبيَّن أنه أخذ الثمن بغير حق؛ لأنه ملك العبد بأداء الضمان، ونفذ بيعه عليه، والثمنُ له دائماً أدّاه إليه على حسبان أنه ملك الراهن، فإذا تبين أنه ملكه لم يكن راضياً به فله أن يرجع به عليه، وإذا رجع بطل الاقتضاء، فيرجع المرتهن على الراهن بدينه. قوله : ورجع ... الخ ؛ أي رجع المشتري على العدل بثمنه ؛ لأنه العاقد، فتعلّق به حقوق العقد، وهذا الرجوع من حقوقه حيث وجب بالبيع، وإنما أدى المشتري الثمن إلى العدل ليسلّم للمشتري المبيع، ولم يسلّم. قوله : على الراهن به ؛ أي بالثمن ؛ لأنه هو الذي أدخله في العهدة، فيجب عليه تخصيصه، وإذا رجع العدلُ على الراهن صح قبض المرتهن ؛ لأنَّ المقبوض سلّم له. قوله : أي على المرتهن ؛ أي إن شاء العدلُ يرجع على المرتهن بثمنه ؛ لأنه إذا انتقض العقد بطل الثمن، وقد قبضه ثمناً ، فيجب نقض قبضه ضرورة، وإذا رجع عليه وانتقض قبضه عادَ حقه في الدين كما كان، فيرجع به على الراهن. ولو أنّ المشتري سلّم الثمن إلى المرتهن لم يرجع على العدل ؛ لأنه في البيع عامل للراهن، وإنما يرجعُ عليه إذا قبض ولم يقبض، فبقي للضمان على الموكل. وإن لم يشترط التوكيل في الرهن رجعَ العدلُ على الراهن فقط، قبض المرتهن ثمنه أو لا ) : أي ما ذكر من خيار العدل بين تضمين الراهن أو المرتهن إنَّما يكون " إذا كانت الوكالة مشروطة في عقدِ الرهن، فإنّه حينئذ تعلق حق المرتهن بالوكالة ، فللعدل تضمين المرتهن ؛ لأنه باعه لحقه. أما إذا لم تكن مشروطة في الرهن تكون كالوكالة المفردة، فإنّه إذا باع الوكيل وأدى الثمن إلى آخر بأمر الموكل ، ثمّ لحقه عهدة لا يرجعُ على القابض، فهاهنا لا يرجعُ إلا على الراهن سواء قبض المرتهن الثمن أو لم يقبض. وصورة ما لم يقبض أنَّ العدلَ باعَ الرهن بأمر الراهن، وضاع الثمنُ في يدِ العدل بلا تعديه ، ثم استحق المرهون ، فالضمان الذي يلحق العدل يرجعُ به على الراهن. قوله : وإن لم يشترط ؛ أي وإن كان التوكيلُ بعد عقد الرهن غير مشروط في العقد عما لحق العدل من العهدة، رجع به العدل على الراهن فقط ، قبض الثمن المرتهن أو لا يقبض ؛ لأنه لم يتعلق بهذا التوكيل حق المرتهن ، فلا رجوع كما في الوكالة المفردة عن الرهن إذا باع الوكيل ودفع الثمنُ إلى مَن أمَرَه الموكَّلُ ثُمَّ لحقه عهدة، لا يرجع به على القابض. بخلاف الوكالة المشروطة في العقد ؛ لأنه تعلّق به حق المرتهن ، فيكون البيع لحقه، وقد سلّم له ذلك جاز أن يلزمه بالضمان ، هكذا يفهم من «الهداية» وشروحه. قوله : إنما يكون ؛ خبر قوله : أي ما ذكر، والمطلب ظاهر، وهذا في التفريق بين الوكالة المشروطة في عقد الرهن والوكالة الغير المشروطة في الرهن الذي ذكره المصنف و الشارح تبعا للكرخي ، حيث ذكره في «مختصره». وهذا يؤيد قول من لا يرى جبر هذا الوكيل على البيع، وقال شمس الأئمة السِّرَخْسِي : هو ظاهر الرواية ؛ لأنَّ رضاء المرتهن بالرهن بدون التوكيل قد تم ، فصار التوكيل مستأنفاً في ضمن عقد الرهن ، فكان منفصلاً عنه ضرورة، على أن فخر الإسلام وشيخ الإسلام الله قالا قول من يرى جبر هذا الوكيل أصح ؛ لإطلاق
And regarding the claimant: he takes it from his purchaser, and he (the purchaser) has recourse against the 'adl for its price, then he (the 'adl) has recourse against the pledgor for it, and the receipt is valid, then he (the 'adl) has recourse against the pledgor for his debt. At that point the 'adl has an option: either to hold the pledgor liable for the value, in which case the sale and receipt of the price are valid, or to hold the mortgagee liable for the price that he paid to him, and it belongs to him; that is, that price becomes for the 'adl, then the mortgagee has recourse against his pledgor for his debt. (And regarding the claimant: he takes it) meaning the person who proves the pawned item belongs to him, from his purchaser, and he (the purchaser) has recourse for its price, then he (the 'adl) has recourse against the pledgor for it, and the receipt is valid) meaning against the mortgagee for its price, (then he (the 'adl) has recourse against the pledgor for his debt) meaning the 'adl has an option: either to have recourse against the pledgor for the price, in which case the mortgagee's receipt of the price is valid, or to have recourse against the mortgagee, then the mortgagee has recourse against the pledgor for his debt. His saying: 'he paid it to him' means because it became clear that he took the price without right, for he owned the slave by paying the guarantee, and his sale is valid, and the price is permanently his; he paid it to him under the assumption that it belonged to the pledgor, so when it became clear that it was his (the 'adl's), he was not satisfied with it, so he has recourse against him for it, and when he has recourse the payment is cancelled, so the mortgagee has recourse against his pledgor for his debt. His saying: 'and he has recourse...' means the purchaser has recourse against the 'adl for his price because he is the contractor, so the rights of the contract are attached to him, and this recourse is among his rights established by the sale, and the purchaser only paid the price to the 'adl to deliver the sold item to him, and it was not delivered. His saying: 'against the pledgor for it' means for the price, because he (the pledgor) is the one who brought him into the liability, so he must indemnify him, and when the 'adl has recourse against the pledgor, the mortgagee's receipt is valid because what was received was delivered to him. His saying: 'i.e. against the mortgagee' means if the 'adl wishes, he has recourse against the mortgagee for his price, because if the contract is nullified, the price is void, and he had received it as a price, so his receipt must necessarily be voided, and when he has recourse and his receipt is voided, his right to the debt returns as it was, so he has recourse against the pledgor for it. And if the purchaser delivered the price to the mortgagee, he does not have recourse against the 'adl, because he (the 'adl) in the sale is acting for the pledgor, and he only has recourse if he received and did not receive, so the liability remains on the principal. And if the agency is not stipulated in the pawn contract, the 'adl has recourse only against the pledgor, whether the mortgagee received his price or not.) That is, what was mentioned regarding the 'adl's option between holding the pledgor or mortgagee liable only applies if the agency was stipulated in the pawn contract; for then the mortgagee's right became attached to the agency, so the 'adl may hold the mortgagee liable because he sold for his right. But if it is not stipulated in the pawn contract, it is like a separate agency; for if the agent sold and paid the price to another by the principal's order, then liability befalls him, he does not have recourse against the recipient; so here he only has recourse against the pledgor, whether the mortgagee received the price or not. The case where he did not receive is that the 'adl sold the pawn by order of the pledgor, and the price was lost in the 'adl's hand without his negligence, then the pawn was reclaimed; then the liability that befalls the 'adl is recoursed against the pledgor. His saying: 'and if it is not stipulated' means if the agency after the pawn contract was not stipulated in the contract, regarding the liability that befell the 'adl, he has recourse against the pledgor only, whether the mortgagee received the price or not; because no right of the mortgagee became attached to this agency, so there is no recourse, as in a separate agency concerning pawn when the agent sells and pays the price to the person ordered by the principal, then liability befalls him, he does not have recourse against the recipient. Contrary to the agency stipulated in the contract, because the mortgagee's right became attached to it, so the sale is for his right, and if that was conceded to him, it is permissible to hold him liable for the guarantee. This is understood from Al-Hidayah and its commentaries. His saying: 'only applies' is the predicate of 'that which was mentioned', and the point is obvious, and this is regarding the distinction between agency stipulated in a pawn contract and agency not stipulated in a pawn contract, which the author and commenter mentioned following al-Karkhi, as he mentioned it in his Mukhtasar. And this supports the saying of those who do not consider this agent to be compelled to sell; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: It is the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya) because the mortgagee's consent to the pawn without agency has been completed, so the agency becomes independent within the pawn contract, thus it is separate from it by necessity. However, Fakhr al-Islam and Shaykh al-Islam [Abu Bakr] said: The saying of those who consider this agent to be compelled to sell is more correct, due to the absolute [nature of the contract].
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling from the chapter on Rahn (pawn) explaining the consequences when a pawned item is sold by the 'adl (trustee) and later reclaimed by a third party (mustahiqq). The passage is an expansion of the base text, distinguishing two scenarios based on whether the agency (wakala) was stipulated in the original pawn contract. The core ruling: The 'adl has an option either to recover the price from the rahin (pledgor) or from the murtahin (mortgagee). This option exists only if the agency was stipulated; otherwise, recourse is solely against the pledgor. The commentary explains each party's recourse: The purchaser sues the 'adl because the 'adl was the direct seller; the 'adl then sues the pledgor or mortgagee depending on the scenario. If the 'adl sues the mortgagee and recovers the price, the mortgagee then sues the pledgor for the original debt. The rationale: If the agency was stipulated, the mortgagee's right is attached to the sale, so he can be held liable. If not stipulated, it is like a separate agency where the agent cannot sue the recipient of the price. The passage concludes with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Sarakhsi holds that such an agent cannot be forced to sell (zahir al-riwaya), while Fakhr al-Islam and Shaykh al-Islam consider the opposite view more correct. The lesson thus covers both the primary ruling and an important secondary dispute within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
العدل (al-‘adl): The trusted third party or trustee who holds the pawned item; he acts as an agent for sale if authorized.
الوكالة المشروطة (al-wakāla al-mashrūṭa): Agency stipulated within the pawn contract; the mortgagee's right becomes attached to it.
الوكالة غير المشروطة (al-wakāla ghayr al-mashrūṭa): Agency not stipulated in the pawn contract; treated like an independent agency.
القائم (al-qā’im): The person who proves ownership of the pawned item and reclaims it from the purchaser; the rightful owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the agency is not stipulated in the pawn contract and the pawned item is reclaimed after sale, against whom does the 'adl have recourse?
A) Only against the mortgagor (pledgor)
B) Only against the mortgagee
C) Either the mortgagor or the mortgagee at the 'adl's option
D) The purchaser

Key Takeaway
The 'adl's option to sue either the pledgor or the mortgagee exists only when the agency to sell was stipulated in the pawn contract; otherwise recourse is solely against the pledgor.

Ruling on Tanned Leather as Pledge and Proportionate Debt Reduction
Explains the ruling on tanned leather as a pledge after the pledged animal dies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportionate debt reduction when a pledged animal dies and its tanned leather becomes a pledge, applying the Hanafi principle of valuing at the time of pledge.

Core Idea
When a pledged sheep dies, the debt is cancelled proportionally to the meat's value, and the tanned leather remains pledged for the remaining debt.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi pledge law: a sheep worth 10 dirhams is pledged for a debt of 10 dirhams, then dies. The meat and skin are separated; the leather is tanned and now worth 1 dirham. The ruling balances the rights of pledgor and mortgagee by proportionally reducing the debt. This teaches us how the value of a pledge is assessed and how partial destruction is handled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
The sheep is worth 10 dirhams and is pledged for a debt of 10 dirhams.
The value of the sheep equals the debt.
2
Understand the event
The sheep dies, its leather is tanned, and the leather is now worth 1 dirham.
The original item is destroyed, but part of it (leather) remains.
3
Apply proportionality
The meat value (9 dirhams) cancels 9 of debt; the leather (1 dirham) remains pledged for the remaining 1 dirham.
For each dirham of the sheep's value, a dirham of debt is dropped.
4
Know the valuation principle
Value is assessed on the day of pledge, not the day of tanning.
The principle is that pledge value is determined at the time the pledge is taken.
5
Extend to other cases
If the sheep's value exceeds the debt, a more detailed rule applies (referenced to al-Kifayah).
This lesson only covers the case where value equals debt.

Source Text
